      This article contains a
      <a href="/wiki/Habesha_name" title="Habesha name">
       Habesha name
      </a>
      . This person is addressed by his given name,
      <b>
       Haile
      </b>
      , and not as
      <b>
       Gebrselassie
      </b>
      the given name of his father.

     <table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;width: 22em;">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <img alt="" data-file-height="120" data-file-width="219" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Ge%27ez.svg/40px-Ge%27ez.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Ge%27ez.svg/60px-Ge%27ez.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Ge%27ez.svg/80px-Ge%27ez.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;">
        <b>
         This article contains
         <a href="/wiki/Ge%27ez_script" title="Ge'ez script">
          Ethiopic text
         </a>
         .
        </b>
        Without proper
        <a href="/wiki/Help:Multilingual_support_(Ethiopic)" title="Help:Multilingual support (Ethiopic)">
         rendering support
        </a>
        , you may see
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Replacement_character" title="Replacement character">
         question marks, boxes, or other symbols
        </a>
        instead of Ethiopic characters.
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      <b>
       Haile Gebrselassie
      </b>
      (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amharic_language" title="Amharic language">
       Amharic
      </a>
      :
      <span lang="am" xml:lang="am">
         
      </span>
      <a href="/wiki/Help:Multilingual_support_(Ethiopic)" title="Help:Multilingual support (Ethiopic)">
       <sup>
        <span class="t nihongo icon" style="color:#00e;font:bold 80% sans-serif;text-decoration:none;padding:0 .1em;">
         ?
        </span>
       </sup>
      </a>
      ,
      <i>
       hayl gebre silass
      </i>
      ; born 18 April 1973) is a retired
      <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">
       Ethiopian
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Long-distance_running" title="Long-distance running">
       long-distance
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Track_running" title="Track running">
       track
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Road_running" title="Road running">
       road running
      </a>
      athlete. He won two Olympic gold medals over
      <a href="/wiki/10,000_metres" title="10,000 metres">
       10,000 metres
      </a>
      and four
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="World Championships in Athletics">
       World Championship
      </a>
      titles in the event. He won the
      <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Marathon" title="Berlin Marathon">
       Berlin Marathon
      </a>
      four times consecutively and also had three straight wins at the
      <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Marathon" title="Dubai Marathon">
       Dubai Marathon
      </a>
      . Further to this, he won four world titles indoors and was the 2001
      <a href="/wiki/IAAF_World_Half_Marathon_Championships" title="IAAF World Half Marathon Championships">
       World Half Marathon Champion
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Haile had major competition wins at distances between
      <a href="/wiki/1500_metres" title="1500 metres">
       1500 metres
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Marathon" title="Marathon">
       marathon
      </a>
      , moving from outdoor, indoor and
      <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">
       cross country running
      </a>
      to road running in the latter part of his career. He broke 61
      <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_records_in_athletics" title="Ethiopian records in athletics">
       Ethiopian national records
      </a>
      ranging from
      <a href="/wiki/800_metres" title="800 metres">
       800 metres
      </a>
      to the marathon, set 27
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_world_records_in_athletics" title="List of world records in athletics">
       world records
      </a>
      , and is widely considered one of the greatest distance runners in history.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In September 2008, at the age of 35, he won the Berlin Marathon with a
      <a href="/wiki/Marathon_world_record_progression" title="Marathon world record progression">
       world record time of 2:03:59
      </a>
      , breaking his own world record by 27 seconds. The record stood for three years. Since he was over the age of 35, that mark still stands as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Masters_Athletics_World_Records" title="Masters Athletics World Records">
       Masters Age group world record
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

        </a>
        <ul>
         <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12">
          <a href="#Outdoor_track">
           <span class="tocnumber">
            4.1
           </span>
           <span class="toctext">
            Outdoor track
           </span>
          </a>
         </li>
         <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">
          <a href="#Road">
           <span class="tocnumber">
            4.2
           </span>
           <span class="toctext">
            Road
           </span>
          </a>
         </li>
         <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14">
          <a href="#Indoor_track">
           <span class="tocnumber">
            4.3
           </span>
           <span class="toctext">
            Indoor track
           </span>
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15">
        <a href="#References">
         <span class="tocnumber">
          5
         </span>
         <span class="toctext">
          References
         </span>
        </a>
       </li>
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16">
        <a href="#External_links">
         <span class="tocnumber">
          6
         </span>
         <span class="toctext">
          External links
         </span>
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>
     </div>
     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Biography">
       Biography
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Haile_Gebrselassie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Biography">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">
       Early career
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Haile_Gebrselassie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early career">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Haile was born as one of ten children in
      <a href="/wiki/Asella" title="Asella">
       Asella
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Oromia_Region" title="Oromia Region">
       Oromia Region
      </a>
      , Ethiopia. As a child growing up on a farm he used to run ten kilometres to school every morning, and the same back every evening. This led to a distinctive running posture, with his left arm crooked as if still holding his school books.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Haile gained international recognition in 1992 when he won the 5000 -metre and 10,000-metre races at the
      <a href="/wiki/1992_World_Junior_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1992 World Junior Championships in Athletics">
       1992 Junior World Championships
      </a>
      in Seoul,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and a silver medal in the junior race at the World Cross Country Championships.
     </p>
     <p>
      The next year, in 1993, Haile won the first of what would eventually be four consecutive world championships titles in the men's 10,000 metres at the
      <a href="/wiki/1993_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1993 World Championships in Athletics">
       1993
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/1995_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1995 World Championships in Athletics">
       1995
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1997 World Championships in Athletics">
       1997
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/1999_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1999 World Championships in Athletics">
       1999
      </a>
      World Championships. His win at the 1993 was however his most infamous as he accidentally stepped on the heel of
      <a href="/wiki/Moses_Tanui" title="Moses Tanui">
       Moses Tanui
      </a>
      's shoe, causing it to fly off his foot. The contact causes Tanui to finish second behind Gebresalassie. Also at the
      <a href="/wiki/1993_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1993 World Championships in Athletics">
       1993 World Championships
      </a>
      he ran in the 5,000-metre race to finish a close second behind
      <a href="/wiki/Ismael_Kirui" title="Ismael Kirui">
       Ismael Kirui
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">
       Kenya
      </a>
      . In 1994 he won a bronze medal at the
      <a href="/wiki/1994_IAAF_World_Cross_Country_Championships" title="1994 IAAF World Cross Country Championships">
       IAAF World Cross Country Championships
      </a>
      . Later that year he set his first world record by running a 12:56.96 in the 5,000-metres, breaking
      <a href="/wiki/Sa%C3%AFd_Aouita" title="Sad Aouita">
       Sad Aouita
      </a>
      's record by two seconds.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haile_Gebrselassie_Hengelo_2009.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="442" data-file-width="640" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Haile_Gebrselassie_Hengelo_2009.JPG/220px-Haile_Gebrselassie_Hengelo_2009.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Haile_Gebrselassie_Hengelo_2009.JPG/330px-Haile_Gebrselassie_Hengelo_2009.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Haile_Gebrselassie_Hengelo_2009.JPG/440px-Haile_Gebrselassie_Hengelo_2009.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haile_Gebrselassie_Hengelo_2009.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Haile competing on the track in
        <a href="/wiki/Hengelo" title="Hengelo">
         Hengelo
        </a>
        , the
        <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
         Netherlands
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1995, Haile ran the 10,000-metres in 26:43.53 in
      <a href="/wiki/Hengelo" title="Hengelo">
       Hengelo
      </a>
      , Netherlands, lowering the world record by nine seconds. That same summer, in
      <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zrich">
       Zrich
      </a>
      , Switzerland, Haile ran the 5000 metres in 12:44.39, taking 10.91 seconds off the world record 12:55.30 (established by Kenya's
      <a href="/wiki/Moses_Kiptanui" title="Moses Kiptanui">
       Moses Kiptanui
      </a>
      earlier in the year). This world record at the
      <a href="/wiki/Weltklasse_Z%C3%BCrich" title="Weltklasse Zrich">
       Weltklasse meet in Zrich
      </a>
      was voted "Performance of the Year" for 1995 by
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Track_%26_Field_News" title="Track &amp; Field News">
        Track &amp; Field News
       </a>
      </i>
      magazine. At the same Weltklasse meet in Zrich in 1996, an exhausted Haile, suffering from blisters obtained on the hard track in
      <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">
       Atlanta
      </a>
      (where he had won the Olympic 10,000 metres gold), had no answer to the 58-second lap of
      <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Komen" title="Daniel Komen">
       Daniel Komen
      </a>
      with five laps to go as Komen went on to win and just miss Haile's record, finishing in 12:45.09. In 1997, Haile turned the tables on Komen at the same meet. Coming off his third 10K world championship gold medal, Haile beat Komen in another Zrich classic on 13 August 1997, covering the final 200 metres in 26.8 seconds to break his 5000 metres world record with a time of 12:41.86.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Komen, in turn, took Haile's record only nine days later when Komen ran a 12:39.74 performance in Belgium.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_career">
       Middle career
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Haile_Gebrselassie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Middle career">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The next year, 1998, saw Haile lowering the indoor world records for 2000 and 3000 metres, enjoying success outdoors by taking back both the 5000 and 10,000 metres world records, as well as earning a share in the Golden League jackpot for winning all of his races in the Golden League series that summer. In June 1998 in
      <a href="/wiki/Hengelo" title="Hengelo">
       Hengelo
      </a>
      , Netherlands, Haile set a
      <a href="/wiki/10,000_metres_world_record_progression" title="10,000 metres world record progression">
       10,000 metres world record
      </a>
      26:22.75, breaking
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tergat" title="Paul Tergat">
       Paul Tergat
      </a>
      's world record 26:27.85, running evenly paced 13:11/13:11 5K splits.
     </p>
     <p>
      Just 13 days later, Haile took on the 5000 metres mark of Komen in
      <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">
       Helsinki
      </a>
      , Finland.
      <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">
       Croatian
      </a>
      pacemaker
      <a href="/wiki/Branko_Zorko" title="Branko Zorko">
       Branko Zorko
      </a>
      took the pace out slowly, hitting 1000 metres in 2:33.91 and dropping out at the mile.
      <a href="/wiki/Million_Wolde" title="Million Wolde">
       Million Wolde
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Assefa_Mezgebu" title="Assefa Mezgebu">
       Assefa Mezgebu
      </a>
      led Haile Gebrselassie through 2000 metres in 5:05.62. His pacemakers could not maintain the pace, though, and Haile was left alone for a difficult solo effort six laps out. Hitting 3000 metres in 7:38.93, even the British commentators announcing the race counted him out. With four laps to go (8:40.00), Haile needed a sub-4-minute final 1,600 metres for the record. With one lap to go and in great pain, Haile took off, recording a final lap of 56.77 seconds and a final 1,600 metres of 3:59.36 (= 4:00.96-mile) to race to a 12:39.36 world record.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1999, Haile starred as himself in the movie
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Endurance_(film)" title="Endurance (film)">
        Endurance
       </a>
      </i>
      . The film chronicled his quest to win Olympic gold in the 10,000 metres in Atlanta. On the track, he won a 1500/3000 metres double at the World Indoor Track Championships, defended his Outdoor World Track Championships 10,000 metres title, and remained undefeated in all his races (which ranged from the 1500 up to 10,000 metres).
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mens_10000m_final_sydney_olympics_2000.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="330" data-file-width="500" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Mens_10000m_final_sydney_olympics_2000.jpg/220px-Mens_10000m_final_sydney_olympics_2000.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Mens_10000m_final_sydney_olympics_2000.jpg/330px-Mens_10000m_final_sydney_olympics_2000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Mens_10000m_final_sydney_olympics_2000.jpg/440px-Mens_10000m_final_sydney_olympics_2000.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mens_10000m_final_sydney_olympics_2000.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Haile (second, in green) on the way to becoming two-time 10,000m Olympic champion in Sydney
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 2000, Haile again won all of his races, ranking first in the world yet again in both the 5000 and 10,000 metres. At the
      <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">
       2000 Sydney Olympics
      </a>
      , he became the third man in history to successfully defend an Olympic 10,000 metres title (after
      <a href="/wiki/Emil_Z%C3%A1topek" title="Emil Ztopek">
       Emil Ztopek
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Lasse_Vir%C3%A9n" title="Lasse Virn">
       Lasse Virn
      </a>
      ). The narrow Olympic victory over Kenya's
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tergat" title="Paul Tergat">
       Paul Tergat
      </a>
      came down to a blistering final kick, with Tergat's 26.3 second final 200 metres being topped by Haile's even faster 25.4. The winning margin of victory was only 0.09 seconds, closer than the winning margin in the men's 100 metre dash final.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2001, Haile won the
      <a href="/wiki/2001_IAAF_World_Half_Marathon_Championships" title="2001 IAAF World Half Marathon Championships">
       IAAF World half marathon
      </a>
      and the bronze medal in the 10,000 metres at the
      <a href="/wiki/2001_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2001 World Championships in Athletics">
       2001 World Championships in Athletics
      </a>
      . In the same year, he also worked with
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Middlebrook" title="Peter Middlebrook">
       Peter Middlebrook
      </a>
      and Abi Masefield he conceptualized the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Ethiopian_Run" title="Great Ethiopian Run">
       Great Ethiopian Run
      </a>
      , which was latterly supported by
      <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Foster" title="Brendan Foster">
       Brendan Foster
      </a>
      , British runner Richard Nerurkar the British ambassador to Ethiopia Myles Wickstead.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 30 August 2003, Haile topped the polls when elected as a member of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IAAF" title="IAAF">
       IAAF
      </a>
      Athletes Commission. Also in 2003, at the World Championships in Paris, Haile was involved in one of the most remarkable 10,000 metres races of all time while gaining a silver medal behind countryman and protg
      <a href="/wiki/Kenenisa_Bekele" title="Kenenisa Bekele">
       Kenenisa Bekele
      </a>
      . The last half of the 10,000 metres final at the championships was completed in a staggering 12:57.24 (12:57.2 for Bekele and 12:58.8 for Haile). According to the IAAF, "Not only was this split the fastest closing 5000 metres in the championships 10,000m (the previous record was 13:12.12, recorded in Atlanta), but it was also the fastest 5000 metres in a global championships surpassing the 12:58.13
      <a href="/wiki/Salah_Hissou" title="Salah Hissou">
       Salah Hissou
      </a>
      recorded when he won the 5,000m in Sevilla'99." (This remark remained true until a week later when the World Athletic Championships 5000 metres medalists (including Bekele) all ran faster than the second 5000 metres split in the previous week's 10,000 metres.) "The difference between the closing 5000 metres splits (12:57.24) and the 5000 metres World record (12:39.36) was 17.98 seconds, which is a record. The previous best of 18.4 seconds (13:31.4 for the closing 5000 metres when the World Record was 13:13.0) was recorded in the 1976 Olympics."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">
       2004 Athens Olympics
      </a>
      , Haile sought to become the first man in history to win three straight Olympic gold medals in the 10,000 metres. He was unable to do so, however, he finished fifth in a race won by his compatriot Kenenisa Bekele, who had broken both of Haile's major track world records, the 5000 metres and the 10,000 metres records. Shortly before the Athens games, Haile was unable to train for three weeks due to inflammation of his
      <a href="/wiki/Achilles_tendon" title="Achilles tendon">
       Achilles tendon
      </a>
      . The injury was severe enough that he would not have competed otherwise, but did so because of significant pressure from his country. This loss of the final period of training likely cost him a medal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Later_career">
       Later career
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Haile_Gebrselassie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Later career">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haile-newyork-cropforfocus.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="737" data-file-width="431" height="427" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Haile-newyork-cropforfocus.jpg/250px-Haile-newyork-cropforfocus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Haile-newyork-cropforfocus.jpg/375px-Haile-newyork-cropforfocus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/94/Haile-newyork-cropforfocus.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haile-newyork-cropforfocus.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Haile in New York in 2003
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Since leaving the track after the 2004 Olympics, Haile has focused on road racing and the marathon. His adult marathons to date include London 2002 (3rd place), Amsterdam 2005 (1st place), London 2006 (9th place), Berlin 2006 (1st place), Fukuoka 2006 (1st place), London 2007 (dnf), Berlin 2007 (1st place and World Record), Dubai 2008 (1st place), Berlin 2008 (1st place and another World Record), Dubai 2009 (1st place) Berlin 2009 (1st place), Dubai 2010 (1st place), and NYC 2010 (dnf).
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2002, Haile made his debut at the marathon at the
      <a href="/wiki/London_Marathon" title="London Marathon">
       London Marathon
      </a>
      . He started the race with a very fast pace, within world record time. He was unable to hold it, however, as world record holder
      <a href="/wiki/Khalid_Khannouchi" title="Khalid Khannouchi">
       Khalid Khannouchi
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tergat" title="Paul Tergat">
       Paul Tergat
      </a>
      both eventually passed him. Khannouchi broke his own world record, while Haile finished third.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="330" data-file-width="500" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg/220px-Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg/330px-Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg/440px-Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Haile shortly before winning the
        <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Marathon" title="Amsterdam Marathon">
         Amsterdam Marathon
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 2005 Haile went undefeated in all of his road races. This included a British All-Comers record in the 10K at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchester,_England" title="Manchester, England">
       Manchester
      </a>
      (27:25), a win in the
      <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Marathon" title="Amsterdam Marathon">
       Amsterdam Marathon
      </a>
      in the fastest marathon time in the world for 2006 (2:06:20), and a new world best for 10 miles in
      <a href="/wiki/Tilburg_Ten_Miles" title="Tilburg Ten Miles">
       Tilburg Ten Miles
      </a>
      race, The Netherlands (44:24). (His unofficial split of 41:22 at the 15K mark was 7 seconds faster than the official world best.)
     </p>
     <p>
      Haile started 2006 positively by beating the world
      <a href="/wiki/Half_marathon" title="Half marathon">
       half marathon
      </a>
      record by a full 21 seconds, recording a time of 58 minutes and 55 seconds on 15 January. He broke the record, his first one on American soil, by running the half marathon of the
      <a href="/wiki/Rock_%27n%27_Roll_Arizona_Marathon" title="Rock 'n' Roll Arizona Marathon">
       Rock 'n' Roll Arizona Marathon
      </a>
      . During the race he also broke Paul Tergat's 20km record, both records having stood since 1998. (Haile passed the 20km mark in 55:48.) That year also marked another victory for Haile as he shattered the 25km world road record (albeit in non-IAAF ratified fashion) by 68 seconds in a time of 1:11.37. The race was organized where Haile and six other runners would run 5 kilometres and then cross the starting line of the 20-K Alphen race in
      <a href="/wiki/Alphen_aan_den_Rijn" title="Alphen aan den Rijn">
       Alphen aan den Rijn
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
       Netherlands
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      On 23 April 2006, he finished ninth in the
      <a href="/wiki/London_Marathon" title="London Marathon">
       London Marathon
      </a>
      with a time of 2:09:05 (the race was won by Kenyan
      <a href="/wiki/Felix_Limo" title="Felix Limo">
       Felix Limo
      </a>
      , who clocked 2:06:39). Haile referred to the ninth-place finish as "the worst race of my career".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, on 24 September he came back with a win in the
      <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Marathon" title="Berlin Marathon">
       Berlin Marathon
      </a>
      in the fastest time of the year, 2:05:56. His time in Berlin made him only the fifth man in history to run under 2:06 for the marathon. This was followed by a win in the
      <a href="/wiki/Fukuoka_Marathon" title="Fukuoka Marathon">
       Fukuoka Marathon
      </a>
      in Japan in 2:06:52.
     </p>
     <p>
      In London on 22 April 2007, Haile challenged the 2006 London Marathon winner
      <a href="/wiki/Felix_Limo" title="Felix Limo">
       Felix Limo
      </a>
      , 2005 London Marathon winner
      <a href="/wiki/Martin_Lel" title="Martin Lel">
       Martin Lel
      </a>
      , 2004 Athens gold medalist
      <a href="/wiki/Stefano_Baldini" title="Stefano Baldini">
       Stefano Baldini
      </a>
      , 2006 New York Marathon winner
      <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADlson_Gomes_dos_Santos" title="Marlson Gomes dos Santos">
       Marlson Gomes dos Santos
      </a>
      , and the then marathon world record holder
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tergat" title="Paul Tergat">
       Paul Tergat
      </a>
      in what organizers anticipated would be an exciting race.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However Haile dropped out at the 18-mile (29km) stage complaining of a
      <a href="/wiki/Side_stitch" title="Side stitch">
       stitch
      </a>
      and inability to breathe, which turned out to be an allergic reaction to the pollen in the air. This left the 2005 winner
      <a href="/wiki/Martin_Lel" title="Martin Lel">
       Martin Lel
      </a>
      to come home in first place.
     </p>
     <p>
      One month later, Haile made a surprise return to the track for the first of two stadium races that summer. In the first, he ran a 26:52.81 in finishing fifth in a very competitive 10,000 metres race in
      <a href="/wiki/Hengelo" title="Hengelo">
       Hengelo
      </a>
      , The Netherlands. Then, on 27 June 2007, Haile launched an attack upon the world record for the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hour_run" title="Hour run">
       one hour run
      </a>
      , in
      <a href="/wiki/Ostrava" title="Ostrava">
       Ostrava
      </a>
      , Czech Republic. This record attempt was successful as Haile passed the hour mark at 21,285metres (13 miles 397 yards), eclipsing the previous best of 21,101metres, set by Mexican
      <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Barrios" title="Arturo Barrios">
       Arturo Barrios
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/La_Fl%C3%A8che" title="La Flche">
       La Flche
      </a>
      , France, on 30 March 1991. Furthermore, Haile covered 50 laps (20,000m) in 56:25.98, another world best, well within the previous 56:55.6 also set by Barrios in 1991. These were his 23rd and 24th world records.
     </p>
     <p>
      Haile made his running debut in New York City when he won the
      <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_Half_Marathon" title="New York City Half Marathon">
       New York City Half Marathon
      </a>
      on 5 August 2007, in 59:24, breaking the previous course record by two minutes. His win in the
      <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Half_Marathon" title="Lisbon Half Marathon">
       Lisbon Half Marathon
      </a>
      (59:15) in March 2008 gave him a perfect record of 90 in winning all of his half marathons. He lost his first half marathon in Den Haag (14 March 2009), when he was beaten by
      <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Kitwara" title="Sammy Kitwara">
       Sammy Kitwara
      </a>
      (59:47 for Kitwara, 59:50 for Haile)
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20090601_Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="518" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/20090601_Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg/220px-20090601_Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/20090601_Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg/330px-20090601_Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/20090601_Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg/440px-20090601_Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20090601_Haile_Gebrselassie.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Haile competing at the 2009
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FBK_Games" title="FBK Games">
         FBK Games
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Hengelo" title="Hengelo">
         Hengelo
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 30 September 2007, Haile won the
      <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Marathon" title="Berlin Marathon">
       Berlin Marathon
      </a>
      in 2:04:26
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (4:44.8 per mile), setting the world record and shaving 29 seconds off
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Tergat" title="Paul Tergat">
       Paul Tergat
      </a>
      's record, set on the same course in 2003. His victory further energized the celebrations of the Ethiopian Millennium (unique to the
      <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_calendar" title="Ethiopian calendar">
       Ethiopian calendar
      </a>
      ), which began on 12 September 2007.
     </p>
     <p>
      Prior to the 2008
      <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Marathon" title="Dubai Marathon">
       Dubai Marathon
      </a>
      , his manager suggested that Haile would be able to run a sub 2:04 time for a new world record. While Haile agreed that a sub 2:04 was possible, he stated that the conditions would need to be perfect for such a time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The event was held on 18 January 2008, and was won by Haile in a time of 2:04:53, making it the second fastest marathon in history. However the early pace had been too fast and he was unable to continue at that speed, resulting in a time 27 seconds short of his own world record.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      At the Hengelo FBK-Games on 24 May, Haile ran 26:51.20 for the 10,000 metres to finish a close second behind countryman
      <a href="/wiki/Sileshi_Sihine" title="Sileshi Sihine">
       Sileshi Sihine
      </a>
      's 26:50.53. Along with his 10,000 meter performances in 2003, 2004, and 2007, Haile is the only man older than 30 years of age to break 27 minutes in the 10,000 metres; his nine career sub 27-minute 10,000 meter performances is more than any other athlete except for Kenenisa Bekele, who also has nine.
     </p>
     <p>
      Because of Beijing's air pollution levels, Haile decided to withdraw from the
      <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_2008_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_marathon" title="Athletics at the 2008 Summer Olympics  Men's marathon">
       marathon
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">
       2008 Beijing Olympics
      </a>
      . He suffers from
      <a href="/wiki/Asthma" title="Asthma">
       asthma
      </a>
      and said that running in such conditions might be harmful for his health.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Haile later admitted that he regretted the decision as the Beijing air was cleaner than expected.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He did, however, run the
      <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_2008_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_10,000_metres" title="Athletics at the 2008 Summer Olympics  Men's 10,000 metres">
       10,000 metres
      </a>
      , finishing sixth with a time of 27:06.68. The gold medal went to his countryman and current world record holder,
      <a href="/wiki/Kenenisa_Bekele" title="Kenenisa Bekele">
       Kenenisa Bekele
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The following month, on 28 September 2008, he defended his Berlin Marathon title, averaging 2:56.5 per kilometer (4:43.7 per mile) for a time of 2:03:59, breaking his own world record by 27 seconds.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haile_2010_Manchester_Run.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1585" data-file-width="1204" height="290" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Haile_2010_Manchester_Run.jpg/220px-Haile_2010_Manchester_Run.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Haile_2010_Manchester_Run.jpg/330px-Haile_2010_Manchester_Run.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Haile_2010_Manchester_Run.jpg/440px-Haile_2010_Manchester_Run.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haile_2010_Manchester_Run.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Haile after winning the 2010
        <a href="/wiki/Great_Manchester_Run" title="Great Manchester Run">
         Great Manchester Run
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Haile won the Dubai Marathon on 16 January 2009, but fell short of breaking his own world record that he had set four months earlier on the flat course. He finished in 2:05:29, well ahead of countryman
      <a href="/wiki/Deressa_Chimsa" title="Deressa Chimsa">
       Deressa Chimsa
      </a>
      . In September that year, he won the Berlin Marathon for the fourth consecutive time. He attempted to break the world record he had set the previous year but, despite a quick start, warm conditions saw him finish in 2:06:08, two minutes away from his best mark. He did, however, pass the 30-kilometer point in 1:27:49, which is a new world record for a road 30K.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2010 he tried to attack his own world record for the third consecutive time at the Dubai Marathon 2010. Although he won the race with a time of 2:06:09, he failed to break his 18-month world record. In a post-race interview he revealed that he had suffered back pain, requiring intensive pre-race physiotherapy, resulting from having slept in a bad position.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His problems continued at the NYC Half Marathon, where he pulled up mid-race visibly uncomfortable in his running.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He had an easy victory in the inaugural edition of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/10K_de_Madrid" title="10K de Madrid">
       10K de Madrid
      </a>
      in April.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He scored his third victory at the Great Manchester Run the following month, although he missed out on Micah Kogo's course record.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He followed this with his first win at the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_North_Run" title="Great North Run">
       Great North Run
      </a>
      in September, finishing the half marathon in a time of 59:33 minutes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      He is also mentor and ambassador for the G4S 4teen, a programme supporting 14 young athletes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_retirement">
       Possible retirement
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Haile_Gebrselassie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Possible retirement">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On 7 November, after dropping out of the
      <a href="/wiki/2010_New_York_City_Marathon" title="2010 New York City Marathon">
       2010 New York City Marathon
      </a>
      with an inflamed knee, Haile announced his retirement.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Days later, he posted to his Twitter account that he was reconsidering his decision and wanted to run in the 2012 London Olympics.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-France-Presse_34-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-France-Presse-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Haile had stated previously that after retiring he would like to enter politics, with scepticism from the public about his knowledge on politics and the unfamiliar culture of celebrities holding public office in
      <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">
       Ethiopia
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However he won his first race back in a 10k road race in Angola with a new course record of 28:05 and beat countryman Deriba Merga and the Kenyan Josphat Menjo who had run the fastest 10000m of that year.
     </p>
     <p>
      Haile missed the 2011
      <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Marathon" title="Tokyo Marathon">
       Tokyo Marathon
      </a>
      due to an injury, but won the
      <a href="/wiki/Half_marathon" title="Half marathon">
       half marathon
      </a>
      at the
      <a href="/wiki/Vienna_City_Marathon" title="Vienna City Marathon">
       Vienna City Marathon
      </a>
      on 17 April 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      About a month later Haile easily won the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Manchester_Run" title="Great Manchester Run">
       Great Manchester Run
      </a>
      in England for the fourth time, finishing in 28:10.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 26 September he suffered a double setback when he dropped out of the Berlin Marathon (again suffering from respiratory difficulties of exercise-induced asthma) and saw his world records for 30 kilometres and the marathon broken by the man with whom he had been duelling,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patrick_Makau" title="Patrick Makau">
       Patrick Makau
      </a>
      . Haile was absent from the press conference later that day, but his manager
      <a href="/wiki/Jos_Hermens" title="Jos Hermens">
       Jos Hermens
      </a>
      announced that while it was "the end of an era of record breaking for Haile, it's not the end of his career".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He returned to his winning ways at the Birmingham half marathon with a new course record and followed that up with a win at the Zevenheuvelenloop in November, taking his third career victory at the Dutch 15K race.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Another outing at the
      <a href="/wiki/Fukuoka_Marathon" title="Fukuoka Marathon">
       Fukuoka Marathon
      </a>
      , however, saw him enter as favourite but drop out at 32km.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2012, Haile ran in the
      <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Marathon" title="Tokyo Marathon">
       Tokyo Marathon
      </a>
      and, after surging to the lead and putting a gap on the field with 6km to go, faded and finished in 4th, in a time of 2:08:17. However, he bounced back to win the Vienna Half Marathon in 1:00:52, catching
      <a href="/wiki/Paula_Radcliffe" title="Paula Radcliffe">
       Paula Radcliffe
      </a>
      who was given a 7:52-minute head-start. He was not selected for the Olympic marathon team, but after winning the
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Manchester_Run" title="Great Manchester Run">
       Great Manchester Run
      </a>
      with a fast time of 27:39, beating marathon world record holder
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patrick_Makau" title="Patrick Makau">
       Patrick Makau
      </a>
      , world marathon leader
      <a href="/wiki/Ayele_Abshero" title="Ayele Abshero">
       Ayele Abshero
      </a>
      and Olympic marathon medallist
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tsegay_Kebede" title="Tsegay Kebede">
       Tsegay Kebede
      </a>
      , by a distance of over 100 metres, he decided to aim for a place in the
      <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_10,000_metres" title="Athletics at the 2012 Summer Olympics  Men's 10,000 metres">
       10,000 m race
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He attempted to earn an Olympic spot at the
      <a href="/wiki/Fanny_Blankers-Koen_Games" title="Fanny Blankers-Koen Games">
       Fanny Blankers-Koen Games
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Hengelo" title="Hengelo">
       Hengelo
      </a>
      , the stadium in which he had broken four world records. However, in extremely hot weather he finished seventh with a time of 27:20.39, sixth amongst Ethiopians, and did not qualify for the
      <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">
       2012 Summer Olympics
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, he did appear at the
      <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2012 Summer Olympics opening ceremony">
       opening ceremony
      </a>
      as one of the eight flagbearers who brought the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_flag" title="Olympic flag">
       Olympic flag
      </a>
      into the stadium.
     </p>
     <p>
      On April 14, 2013, Gebrselassie won the open field of the Vienna City half marathon (13.1 miles) with a time of 01:01.14. He set his first over-40 world record with a time of 46:59 for 10 miles in Switzerland, on 15 September 2013. He took 3rd overall in the 2013 BUPA Great North Run, 32 seconds behind the winner Kenenisa Bekele and 31 seconds behind the reigning Olympic and world champion Mo Farah.
     </p>
     <p>
      Haile Gebrselassie has announced his retirement from competitive running after finishing 16th in the Great Manchester Run on Sunday May 10 2015. It brings to an end a 25-year career in which he claimed two Olympic gold medals, eight World Championship victories and set 27 world records. "I'm retiring from competitive running, not from running. You cannot stop running, this is my life," he told BBC Sport.Gebrselassie remains the world record holder at 20,000m and the one-hour race.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Achievements">
       Achievements
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">

       </a>

       </span>
      </span>

        <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">

        , United States
       </td>
